0.25em 1em; line-height: 1.5em;">\n         Release\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Original network\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_syndication" title="Broadcast syndication">\n          Syndication\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Original release\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         September 12, 1988\n         <span style="display:none">\n          (\n          <span class="bday dtstart published updated">\n           1988-09-12\n          </span>\n          )\n         </span>\n         \xe2\x80\x93 January 7, 1990\n         <span style="display:none">\n          (\n          <span class="dtend">\n           1990-01-07\n          </span>\n          )\n         </span>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th class="summary" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #CCCCFF; padding: 0.25em 1em; line-height: 1.5em;">\n         External links\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Website\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <span class="url">\n          <a class="external text" href="https://www.usatoday.com/" rel="nofollow">\n           www\n           <wbr/>\n           .usatoday\n           <wbr/>\n           .com\n          </a>\n         </span>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       In 1987, Gannett and producer\n       <a href="/wiki/Grant_Tinker" title="Grant Tinker">\n        Grant Tinker\n       </a>\n       began developing a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newsmagazine" title="Newsmagazine">\n        newsmagazine\n       </a>\n       series for\n       <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_syndication" title="Broadcast syndication">\n        first-run syndication\n       </a>\n       that attempted to bring the breezy style of\n       <i>\n        USA Today\n       </i>\n       to television.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The result was\n       <i>\n        USA Today: The Television Show\n       </i>\n       (later retitled\n       <i>\n        USA Today on TV\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       then shortened to simply\n       <i>\n        USA Today\n       </i>\n       ), which premiered on September 12, 1988.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Correspondents on the program included Edie Magnus,\n       <a href="/wiki/Robin_Young" title="Robin Young">\n        Robin Young\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Boyd_Matson" title="Boyd Matson">\n        Boyd Matson\n       </a>\n       , Kenneth Walker, Dale Harimoto, Ann Abernathy,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bill_Macatee" title="Bill Macatee">\n        Bill Macatee\n       </a>\n       and Beth Ruyak. As with the newspaper itself, the show was divided into four "sections" corresponding to the different parts of the paper: News (focusing on the major headlines of the day), Money (focusing on financial news and consumer reports), Sports (focusing on sports news and scores) and Life (focusing on entertainment and lifestyle-related stories).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The series was plagued by low ratings and negative reviews from critics throughout its run. The program also suffered from being scheduled in undesirable timeslots in certain markets; this was a particular case in\n       <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">\n        New York City\n       </a>\n       , the country\'s largest\n       <a href="/wiki/Media_market" title="Media market">\n        media market\n       </a>\n       , where CBS\n       <a href="/wiki/Owned-and-operated_station" title="Owned-and-operated station">\n        owned-and-operated station\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/WCBS-TV" title="WCBS-TV">\n        WCBS-TV\n       </a>\n       (channel 2) aired the program in a pre-dawn early morning slot, before the program moved to NBC O&amp;O\n       <a href="/wiki/WNBC" title="WNBC">\n        WNBC\n       </a>\n       five months into its run in a 9:30\xc2\xa0a.m. slot, where it did not fare any better despite being placed in a more palatable time period\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       (in contrast,\n       <a href="/wiki/CITY-DT" title="CITY-DT">\n        CITY-TV\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">\n        Toronto\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">\n        Ontario\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">\n        Canada\n       </a>\n       [now the\n       <a href="/wiki/Flagship_(broadcasting)" title="Flagship (broadcasting)">\n        flagship station\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/City_(TV_network)" title="City (TV network)">\n        City\n       </a>\n       television network], ran it at 5:00\xc2\xa0p.m.).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ) These setbacks led to the cancellation of the TV version of\n       <i>\n        USA Today\n       </i>\n       in November 1989 after one-and-a-half seasons; the final edition aired on January 7, 1990.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Gannett announced plans to develop a\n       <i>\n        USA Today\n       </i>\n       -branded weekly half-hour television program, to have been titled "Sports Page", as part of a renewed initiative to extend the brand into television; this program, which was tapped for a fall 2004 debut, ultimately never launched.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday30.usatoday_9-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-usatoday30.usatoday-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="VRtually_There">\n        <i>\n         VRtually There\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=USA_Today&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: VRtually There">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        VRtually There\n       </i>\n       is a weekly\n       <a href="/wiki/Virtual_reality" title="Virtual reality">\n        virtual reality\n       </a>\n       news program produced by the USA Today Network, which debuted on October 20, 2016. The program, which is available on the\n       <i>\n        USA Today\n       </i>\n       mobile app and on\n       <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">\n        YouTube\n       </a>\n       (which maintains content exclusivity through the program\'s dedicated channel for 60 days after each broadcast), showcases three original segments outlining news stories through a first-person perspective, recorded and produced by journalists from\n       <i>\n        USA Today\n       </i>\n       and its co-owned local newspapers. The program also incorporates "cubemercials," long-form advertisements created by Gannett\'s in-house creative studio GET Creative, which are designed to allow consumer engagenent in fully immersive experiences through virtual reality.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">\n        Awards\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=USA_Today&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Awards">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/USA_Today_Minor_League_Player_of_the_Year_Award" title="USA Today Minor League Player of the Year Award">\n         USA Today Minor League Player of the Year Award\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 First presented in 1988, this annual award has been given to a particular\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minor_league_baseball" title="Minor league baseball">\n         Minor League Baseball\n        </a>\n        player judged to have had the most outstanding season by a thirteen-person panel of baseball experts.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/USA_Today_All-USA_high_school_baseball_team" title="USA Today All-USA high school baseball team">\n         USA Today All-USA high school baseball team\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 First presented in 1998, the award honors between nine and eleven outstanding baseball players from high schools around the United States to be part on the team (separate awards honoring the High School Baseball Player of the Year and High School Baseball Coach of the Year have been given since 1989\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BaseballPlayersAndCoaches_66-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-BaseballPlayersAndCoaches-66">\n          [66]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday7_67-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-usatoday7-67">\n          [67]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        ).\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/USA_Today_All-USA_high_school_basketball_team" title="USA Today All-USA high school basketball team">\n         USA Today All-USA high school basketball team\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 First presented in 1983, the award honors outstanding male and female basketball players from high schools around the United States with a place on the team, with one member of each team being named as the High School Basketball Player of the Year as well as coaches from a select boys\' and girls\' team as the High School Basketball Coach of the Year.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday7_67-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-usatoday7-67">\n          [67]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday7_67-2">\n         <a href="#cite_note-usatoday7-67">\n          [67]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n         <a href="#cite_note-68">\n          [68]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n         <a href="#cite_note-69">\n          [69]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=USA_Today_All-Joe_Team&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="USA Today All-Joe Team (page does not exist)">\n         USA Today All-Joe Team\n        </a>\n        (NFL) \xe2\x80\x93 First presented in 1992 in tribute to\n        <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Chiefs" title="Kansas City Chiefs">\n         Kansas City Chiefs\n        </a>\n        veteran defensive lineman\n        <a href="/wiki/Joe_Phillips" title="Joe Phillips">\n         Joe Phillips\n        </a>\n        , the award honors 52 rookie players from throughout the NFL for their exemplary performance during the previous league season.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n         <a href="#cite_note-70">\n          [70]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         USA Today\n        </i>\n        /National Prep Poll\n        <a href="/wiki/High_School_Football_National_Championship" title="High School Football National Championship">\n         High School Football National Championship\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 Predating the first publication of\n        <i>\n         USA Today\n        </i>\n        under the sole decision of the National Prep Poll, it is a national championship honor awarded to the best\n        <a href="/wiki/High_school_football" title="High school football">\n         high school football\n        </a>\n        team(s) in the United States based on rankings decided by\n        <i>\n         USA Today\n        </i>\n        <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\n         \'\n        </span>\n        s sports editorial department.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/USA_Today_All-USA_high_school_football_team" title="USA Today All-USA high school football team">\n         USA Today All-USA high school football team\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 First presented in 1982, the award honors outstanding football players from high schools around the United States (includes ranks for the Super 25 teams in the U.S. and Top 10 teams in the East, South, Midwest and West, and\n        <a href="/wiki/USA_Today_High_School_Football_Player_of_the_Year" title="USA Today High School Football Player of the Year">\n         USA Today High School Football Player of the Year\n        </a>\n        ).\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n         <a href="#cite_note-71">\n          [71]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n         <a href="#cite_note-72">\n          [72]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USA_Today_High_School_Football_Coach_of_the_Year" title="USA Today High School Football Coach of the Year">\n         USA Today High School Football Coach of the Year\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 First presented in 1982, the award awards a coach from one of the teams selected for the All-USA football team for the honor.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">\n        In popular culture\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=USA_Today&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: In popular culture">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USA_Today_BTTF_Logo.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="120" data-file-width="200" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/d/d7/USA_Today_BTTF_Logo.png" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USA_Today_BTTF_Logo.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The futuristic Logo used in\n         <i>\n          Back to the Future Part II\n         </i>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A futuristic 2015 edition of\n       <i>\n        USA Today\n       </i>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Hill_Valley_(Back_to_the_Future)" title="Hill Valley (Back to the Future)">\n        Hill Valley\n       </a>\n       edition) is seen in\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_Part_II" title="Back to the Future Part II">\n         Back to the Future Part II\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (1989). As a tribute to the movie, the newspaper ran a recreation of the front page, featuring the exact headlines portrayed in the movie, on October 22, 2015, the exact date of the edition that the protagonist Marty McFly read in the movie (the character, played by\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_J._Fox" title="Michael J. Fox">\n        Michael J. Fox\n       </a>\n       , travels to October 21, 2015, and reads the following day\'s edition of the paper.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span
